<div id="review_1114978693" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1114978693" />
    <a title="Jokoloyo" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1902630-jokoloyo"><img alt="Jokoloyo" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1423473158p2/1902630.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1114978693?book_show_action=true">Nov 24, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jokoloyo" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jokoloyo" href="/user/show/1902630-jokoloyo">Jokoloyo</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1114978693" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16952305248714750750">For my individual taste, this novel is mystery first, fantasy second. As a mystery novel, I am not so satisfied with the plot and conclusion. As a fantasy novel, it is a damn good one!<br/><br/>When I read the beginning, I rated it 3 star. Then at the middle, I like the fantasy portion more and more, rated it 4 star. I have to admit, there are fresh ideas about the magic (in the book, the magic is mentioned as miracles). After reading half of the book, I wanted to know more about the world. This book gave</span>
  <span id="freeText16952305248714750750" style="display:none">For my individual taste, this novel is mystery first, fantasy second. As a mystery novel, I am not so satisfied with the plot and conclusion. As a fantasy novel, it is a damn good one!<br><br>When I read the beginning, I rated it 3 star. Then at the middle, I like the fantasy portion more and more, rated it 4 star. I have to admit, there are fresh ideas about the magic (in the book, the magic is mentioned as miracles). After reading half of the book, I wanted to know more about the world. This book gave me more and more revelation with about the world, and I like it more and more. The climax and conclusion are satisfactory. Solid 5 star for the world building. One of the interesting world building is the city itself. The stairs are not exotic views, but there is some meaning.<br><br> <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1498206074i/23104657._SX540_.jpg" alt="cityofstairs4" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>(I get it from soipondered.files.wordpress.com)<br><br>I usually don't give too much thinking in fantasy, but with mystery as the main plot, I read every fantasy factor as a clue. I blame the plot that made me thought so much and eventually detected some foreshadowing. I was not too surprised for some aspect of the novel. (OK, I am exaggerating my intelligence. Some foreshadows are so obvious, I believe every reader could detect them easily).<br><br>The characters are pretty solid. At least, this novel passed Bechdel Test, with so many good conversations between female characters (Majority of the important characters in this novel are female).<br><br>Using a mystery plot for a fantasy novel is a brave choice for the author. The main reason I read this novel is the curiosity how this novel could blend mystery and fantasy. After reading the end this novel, I think it is not a true mystery story. I wish this novel could use more mystery routines to make it a good true mystery story, it has so much potential.<br><br>If I read this novel mainly as a fantasy novel, it is an easy 5-star. But I read it as a mystery, I demand more clues/foreshadows that on par with mystery novels. With that kind of reading attitude, I believe readers could detect the foreshadowing parts, and guess the plot twists at later parts of the novel.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16952305248714750750" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Deborah by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/59458347-petrik">Petrik</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54790180-deborah-obida?shelf=adult">adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54790180-deborah-obida?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2787297246" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8079052319045417432"><b>
  <i>“I never saw a country before," says the robed man. "All I saw was the earth under my feet.” </i>
</b><br/><br/>Now that is what I call original, This book is one of those books that has more than one genre, I don't even know how to shelve it, I'm shelving it as urban fantasy even though it felt like epic fantasy but the technology ruined that. There also used guns in this so this is more of historical fiction I guess.<br/><br/><b>
  <i>“Forgetting... is a beautiful thing. When you forget, you remake yourself... For a caterpi</i></b></span>
  <span id="freeText8079052319045417432" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>“I never saw a country before," says the robed man. "All I saw was the earth under my feet.” </i>
</b><br /><br />Now that is what I call original, This book is one of those books that has more than one genre, I don't even know how to shelve it, I'm shelving it as urban fantasy even though it felt like epic fantasy but the technology ruined that. There also used guns in this so this is more of historical fiction I guess.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>“Forgetting... is a beautiful thing. When you forget, you remake yourself... For a caterpillar to become a butterfly, it must forget it was a caterpillar at all. Then it will be as if the caterpillar never was &amp; there was only ever a butterfly.” </i>
</b><br /><br />The first few pages of this book was tedious, but after Shara came everything changed. I really enjoyed her POV, hers and Sigrud. The way the author integrated the past into the present was awesome, knowing about Shara and Sigrud's past was awesome. I had to admit I wasn't wowed by the world building, it was confusing sometimes, I guess its because of the nature of the buildings in Bulikov.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>“Humans are strange. … They value punishment because they think it means their actions are important—that they are important. … it's vanity.” </i>
</b><br /><br />The characters are lovable, I'm torn between Sigrud and Shara who my favourite is, despite their crazy past, his more crazier than hers they became friends. I also like Vohannes, he's outright amazing. Mugladesh the governor isn't too bad either.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>“Just because the nightmare you expected comes true, it doesn't make it any less terrifying.”</i>
</b><br /><br />The plot is more of a murder mystery with a dash of archaeology and dead gods. The city of Bulikov was once the centre of the world where gods live, it was more like the capital. Whatever the gods wanted happened, they replace reality with their own, the city was so beautiful but everything changed when the Saypuri attacked. Now the city is impoverished, the buildings are a wreck, people are starving and dying. <br /><br />Some thousands years later one of Saypur's historian got murdered in Bulikov, Shara is sent to investigate and she found more than she bargained for.</span>

<div id="review_1524567929" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1524567929" />
    <a title="Gavin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8192509-gavin"><img alt="Gavin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1338207884p2/8192509.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1524567929?book_show_action=true">Jan 25, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Gavin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Gavin" href="/user/show/8192509-gavin">Gavin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8192509-gavin?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1524567929" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7742127588994071144"><i>And Olvos said to them: “Why have you done this, my children? Why is the sky wreathed with smoke? Why have you made war in far places, and shed blood in strange lands?”<br/>And they said to Her: “You blessed us as Your people, and we rejoiced, and were happy. But we found those who were not Your people, and they would not become Your people, and they were willful and ignorant of You. They would not open their ears to Your songs, or lay Your words upon their tongues. So we dashed them upon the rocks a</i></span>
  <span id="freeText7742127588994071144" style="display:none"><i>And Olvos said to them: “Why have you done this, my children? Why is the sky wreathed with smoke? Why have you made war in far places, and shed blood in strange lands?”<br />And they said to Her: “You blessed us as Your people, and we rejoiced, and were happy. But we found those who were not Your people, and they would not become Your people, and they were willful and ignorant of You. They would not open their ears to Your songs, or lay Your words upon their tongues. So we dashed them upon the rocks and threw down their houses and shed their blood and scattered them to the winds, and we were right to do so. For we are Your people. We carry Your blessings. We are Yours, and so we are right. Is this not what You said?”<br />And Olvos was silent.</i><br /><br />This is the fantastic intro to the unique and thought provoking fantasy story that is City of Stairs. On the surface Robert Jackson Bennett's tale is a murder mystery set in a very original fantasy setting, but just below the surface the book deals with all sorts of issues such as slavery, oppression, censorship, fanaticism (both religious and patriotic), social unrest, and moral dilemmas questioning just what is acceptable in the name of the "greater good". It all made for an interesting read and Bennett's engaging writing style and down to earth characters made sure the story was every bit as engaging as it was interesting.<br /><br />The world building was excellent. The late 19th Century setting is underutilized in secondary world fantasy books and gave this story a fresh feel. The mythology of the Divinities was cool and the histories and cultures of the various nations and people were well drawn. The only flaw I had with the world building was the fact that descriptions of Bulikov itself was pretty sparse. Luckily I found <a href="http://www.robertjacksonbennett.com/wp-content/uploads/2014/09/CityOfBulikov.htm" rel="nofollow noopener">this</a> fantastic page on the authors website that had some great art of the city of Bulikov! <br /><br />All in all I found this to be an original and enjoyable read.<br /><br />Rating: 4.5 stars.<br /><br />Audio Note: Alma Cuervo did a good job with the audio.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7742127588994071144" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3129077086" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3129077086" />
    <a title="Aoife - Bookish_Babbling" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/22314328-aoife---bookish-babbling"><img alt="Aoife - Bookish_Babbling" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1554984281p2/22314328.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3129077086?book_show_action=true">Feb 03, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Aoife - Bookish_Babbling" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Aoife - Bookish_Babbling" href="/user/show/22314328-aoife---bookish-babbling">Aoife - Bookish_Babbling</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/23307808-city-of-stairs">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22314328-aoife---bookish-babbling?shelf=read-in-2020">read-in-2020</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3129077086" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8471130448931329854">TLDR<br/>Solid 4*<br/>Interesting read unlike any fantasy world I've read before, the MCs interactions made it for me.<br/>Fun twists & reveals, but I saw most of them coming so while it was a very enjoyable read it didn't quite knock my socks off. Still highly recommend 😇<br/><br/>******<br/><br/>Politics & religion are not typically subjects I seek out when looking for books to read. However the way these were tackled and slowly unveiled to us, like peeling back the layers of an onion through the opening act of a murder mystery</span>
  <span id="freeText8471130448931329854" style="display:none">TLDR<br />Solid 4*<br />Interesting read unlike any fantasy world I've read before, the MCs interactions made it for me.<br />Fun twists &amp; reveals, but I saw most of them coming so while it was a very enjoyable read it didn't quite knock my socks off. Still highly recommend 😇<br /><br />******<br /><br />Politics &amp; religion are not typically subjects I seek out when looking for books to read. However the way these were tackled and slowly unveiled to us, like peeling back the layers of an onion through the opening act of a murder mystery...well it had me hooked!<br />Once the main characters of Shara, Sigrud, Mulaghesh &amp; even Vo were layered in and we got to see them interact I was sold. Especially the friendships between the first 3, I am 100% invested in each and every one of them &amp; could read their conversations and interactions all day 👍<br /><br />Shara was such an interesting MC, yes she knew everything we needed to know but she like us had to piece things together as she went along, through her the info we all needed was revealed. Unlike <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2790635155" rel="nofollow noopener">Foundryside</a> where I found the necessary intel to be info dumpy &amp; heavy handed. The revelations came about in a much more manageable way in this earlier series, which is almost a funny turnaround as usually it is the reverse for authors and the later series tend to reveal things more smoothly to the reader.<br />Sigrud &amp; Mulaghesh are just amazing and need to be discovered as you read because they were such delightfully destructive gems 😎<br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<br />Vo's appearances were also entertaining &amp; he deffo brought some unexpected representation to this book that I hadn't anticipated, but to me, it was so background that it almost seems like a bit of an afterthought ... I'm prob being harsh there tho, not my rep so I shouldn't comment and really it was an interestingly refreshing, I hesitate to say "twist" as it's not really something that should be a plot ploy - but it did add an interesting layer to Vo's character and took the storyline in a slightly different direction than one might typically think it would go...in saying that tho I just felt like it was not really explored in a meaningful way but it did allow for displays of understanding and I guess it exhibited the differing ideologies of the cultures being represented in this world. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Speaking of representation, perhaps I am way off the mark here but I really enjoyed the ethnic representation of our MC, that I for one, have not previously had the pleasure to see much in fantasy settings.<br />I also quite liked how the storyline didn't shy away from the bitterness and resentment festering in/on both sides from the change in fortunes which led to the reversal of oppressions and although obviously not solved by the end of the book hopefully steps will be taken in the right direction to avoid making the same mistakes going forward.<br /><br />The ending, while very satisfying &amp; the desired result deffo didn't go quite as I'd thought it would. I expected more resistance from a certain character, but I guess the wind was completely knocked out of their sails? *shrug*<br />This was a 4.25* read last night but that final part just knocked some of the shine off for me after quite the action packed build up &amp; reveals just before it.<br />However I am curious to see what the main players get up to in the next books and hope for more interactions between them as much as possible 😈 <br /><br />The idea &amp; role of the Divinities was such an interesting take in this fantasy world. We come into the story 70odd years after their defeat at the hands of a previously colonised and repressed people. Prior to this these Divinities ruled with the aid of "miracles" which contributed greatly to the everyday life of their followers and supported everything from buildings to plumbing and seriously stunted any technological advances the people of the Continent might otherwise have made, and that indeed their colonies did make (as they were not divinely blessed).<br />Needless to say the world the Divinities created literally fell apart at their defeat and the people who worshiped them &amp; thrived under their patronage were not only greatly saddened by their loss and those that perished in the war/cataclysm known as the Blink. But also the loss of stature in the world and they understandably chafe at their reversal of fortunes...it is hard to do justice to the description of this really interesting set up and we haven't even touched upon all the tasty reveals and twists this book springs upon the reader.<br /><br />Just do yourself a favour &amp; pick this up - I hope you won't be disappointed 😅<br /><br />PS - I don't think the Divinity talk above is a spoiler as I for one would have been mighty confused if I hadn't had some semblance of an understanding as to their roles before this book starts because we get tossed in the deep end with the first chapter cold opening during a court case.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8471130448931329854" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('ghf+01NrS/Euh2R39Q/o1xtrEU3yVrOYS1v8ODCwHTtYLR8uUauMbFeCZTI3wC+0sFm0ki53ryzyxLhF5s081A==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('bGrMEtq0XB/OAxnNl7WQKdTK6DMGtPLC2kxi5jQH48e2UC3v2HSbgrcGGIhVeldKf/hN7NqV7nZj0yab4nrCKA==')})
  }

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer16568842922219734479">Robert Jackson Bennett is a two-time award winner of the Shirley Jackson Award for Best Novel, an Edgar Award winner for Best Paperback Original, and is also the 2010 recipient of the Sydney J Bounds Award for Best Newcomer, and a Philip K Dick Award Citation of Excellence. City of Stairs was shortlisted for the Locus Award and the World Fantasy Award. City of Blades was a finalist for the 2015 Wo</span>
  <span id="freeText16568842922219734479" style="display:none">Robert Jackson Bennett is a two-time award winner of the Shirley Jackson Award for Best Novel, an Edgar Award winner for Best Paperback Original, and is also the 2010 recipient of the Sydney J Bounds Award for Best Newcomer, and a Philip K Dick Award Citation of Excellence. City of Stairs was shortlisted for the Locus Award and the World Fantasy Award. City of Blades was a finalist for the 2015 World Fantasy, Locus, and British Fantasy Awards. His eighth novel, FOUNDRYSIDE, will be available in the US on 8/21 of 2018 and the UK on 8/23.</span>

      <div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/work/quotes/28030792-city-of-stairs">Quotes from City of Stairs</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class="stacked" tyle="padding-bottom:15px">
            <span class="readable">&ldquo;<i>And Olvos said to them: “Why have you done this, my children? Why is the sky wreathed with smoke? Why have you made war in far places, and shed blood in strange lands?<br /><br />And they said to Her: “You blessed us as Your people, and we rejoiced, and were happy. But we found those who were not Your people, and they would not become Your people, and they were willful and ignorant of You. They would not open their ears to Your songs, or lay Your words upon their tongues. So we dashed them upon the rocks and threw down their houses and shed their blood and scattered them to the winds, and we were right to do so. For we are Your people. We carry Your blessings. We are Yours, and so we are right. Is this not what You said?”<br /><br />And Olvos was silent.</i>&rdquo;</span>

For a caterpillar to become a butterfly, it must forget it was a caterpillar at all. Then it will be as if the caterpillar never was &amp; there was only ever a butterfly.&rdquo;</span>
